"HCNKWQSIJT";"The standard weapon for a large number of frontline soldiers, the battle rifle is effective against enemy troops at intermediate ranges.\nHeavy and powerful, battle rifles are very accurate and deadly when the shooter is immobile, but quite less than an assault rifle on the move, especially since it uses smaller magazines. Most assault rifles can be modified with accessories such as scopes, foregrips, night vision devices, or single-shot grenade launchers."

"HISBEL16PD";"The 16e Pantserdivisie, or 16th Armored Division, was one of the two original formations of the Belgian Army’s I (BE) Corps, forward deployed in NORTHAG from 1951. While Belgium never wavered in its commitment to NATO, for most of the Cold War, its underfunded bilingual armed forces were regarded as one of the least powerful in the alliance. By the end of the 1980s, however, serious efforts were made to modernize and introduce new weaponry in the Belgian Armed Forces.\n\nClose to a mechanized infantry formation, the 16e Pantserdivisie is reinforced with well-trained reconnaissance troops. It also includes Luxembourg's diminutive contribution to NATO: a light infantry battalion equipped with American-made materiel. One of the most recent Belgian acquisitions is the AIFV armored vehicle family, transporting Mech. Fusiliers infantry. Armor support takes the form of the Leopard 1 (BE), including the rare Leopard 1A5 (BE). The division’s recon forces are prolific users of the CRV(T) family of vehicles, from Spartan to Scimitar light tanks, backed by ESR special forces available as 6-man recon or 2-man sniper teams. A handful A.109HA helicopters have been pressed into active service, which, together with the Gepard 2B SPAAGs, Épervier UAVs, Mistral AA MANPADS, and the Belgian Air Force’s F-16A with HE and Cluster payloads, constitute some of the most advanced equipment of the Belgian Army."
"HISBELDIMO";"The Division Mobilisation was the Belgian Army’s umbrella designation for various interior troops called upon to reinforce I (BE) Corps in West Germany in case of conflict. If an enemy breakthrough or airborne assaults threatened Belgian territory directly, this NATO rear-area formation would also provide local security for key sites and army assets. Division Mobilisation included a collection of Territorial regiments, regular light infantry, plus Gendarmerie military police and its armored squadron, plus shadowy stay-behind special forces. Older stockpiled equipment from weapon depots, as well as heavy anti-air units, would also fall under the division’s command.\n\nThe Division Mobilisation, while fielding older weaponry, is a mechanized battlegroup at heart. This includes the light M41 tank, the heavier M47 main battle tank, M75 APC and command vehicle, BDX wheeled APCs, plus FN 4RM 62F Gendarmerie armored vehicles. Chasseurs Ardennais light infantry will deploy side-by-side with False Flag-traited SDRA8 saboteur squads. Artillery ranges from the World War II-era Long Tom 155mm and M1 8-inch 203mm howitzers to slightly more modern M108A2 105mm and M55 203mm self-propelled units. Potent anti-air cover is provided by HSS.630-3 triple 20mm and Bofors M/54 57mm heavy AA guns, and I-Hawk SAM."
"HISCAN1ID";"The 1st Canadian Division had a distinguished combat record spanning both World Wars, though it was mostly inactive during the Cold War. Reactivation came in 1988, when the formation was used to consolidate the Canadian land forces based in Lahr, southern West Germany. The overarching Canadian Forces Europe, including the 1st Canadian Air Division, was to be placed under French command of SOUTHAG in case of war.\n\nThe 1st Canadian Division counts on two infantry brigades, the heavy 4 Canadian Mechanized Brigade-Group, and the much lighter 5e Groupe-Brigade Mécanisé du Canada. Infantry follow their parent brigade in strength and mobility, from Mech. Rifles, Tank Hunters, CFMP military police, or Reserve squads with Canadian-designated small arms. They deploy in either tracked M113 or wheeled Grizzly APCs, including a rare Grizzly CP escort. Canada’s main battle tank in the late Cold War is the Leopard C1, a Leopard 1A3 upgraded with more accurate fire-control systems. Another interesting unit is the Cougar, acting as a fire support vehicle. The fast CL-89 drone provides valuable eyes in the sky, while the unique ADATS fires dual-ATGM and AA missiles. The Royal Canadian Air Force fields the state-of-the-art CF-18 (F-18) in a variety of different load-outs, backed by CF-5A, Silver Star MK.3AT trainers, and EF-101B Electric Voodoo EW planes."
"HISCZ19MD";"The Czechoslovak People’s Army 19. Motostřelecká Divize, or 19th Motor Rifle Division, was created in 1958 in Plzeň, its home base for the duration of the Cold War. The ČSLA’s motorized rifle division, much like other Warsaw Pact allies, was structured along the Soviet Army lines. In the event of war, reorganizations would see the 19th Motorized lose one of its infantry regiments but, in turn, gain the famous 22nd Airborne Brigade and a helicopter regiment. \n\nThe 19. Motostřelecká Divize features a strong core of logistical and command units, from the T813 heavy supply truck to the OT-62/R4MT command APC. They serve the capable but limited number of Motostřelci mechanized infantry, backed by a handful of elite airborne Výsadkáři special forces, including weapon teams equipped with recoilless rifles, Igla AA, and Konkurs ATGMs. Supporting arms, such as artillery with its domestically-made Dana self-propelled howitzers, the 120mm mortar-carrying Prám-S and the long-range SHK 2S7, can deploy side-by-side with T-72M1 tanks, advanced T-55AM1s, OT PTRK Konkurs tank destroyers, and PLRK Kub mobile SAMs. Several other potent units round out the divisional arsenal, including the dual-Jammer and SIGINT-traited Mi-17Z2 helicopter, MiG-29 air defense fighters, the Su-25 ground attack aircraft in large numbers, and the Mi-24V gunship in various configurations."
"HISCZ1TD";"The 1. Tanková Divize, or 1st Tank Division, was formed in 1958 by the Československá ľudová armáda or Czechoslovak People’s Army (ČSLA). The ČSLA’s political allegiance to the socialist cause was seriously questioned after the Prague Spring of 1968, with low morale and strict Soviet oversight still felt by the late 1980s. However, thanks to Czechoslovakia’s well-established industrial base, its armed forces were considered one of the best-equipped in the Warsaw Pact, from small arms to IFVs and aircraft. \n\nThe 1. Tanková Divize, as part of the ČSLA’s 1st Army, was to be used as a well-trained exploitation force. The division’s mechanized troops rely heavily on the capable T-72M, including the T-72S, and the BMP-2, both produced domestically under license. Regular Motostřelci infantry and Ženist combat engineers can also deploy in BVP-1 and OT-64 APCs (Polish-made SKOT). The division’s artillery forces are well-equipped, ranging from M Vz.52 82mm mortars, self-propelled SH M 2S4 Tulipan 240mm mortars, and an SVO demining vehicle with its massive, 240mm short-range mine-clearing rockets. Recon is another category that shines, with units such as SHPZ recon special forces, BPVZ Svatava radar-recon, and the Tu-143 recon drone. The Československé letectvo, or Czechoslovak Air Force, deploys either the MiG-23BN with a variety of ground strike payloads or MiG-23MLA in an air defense role."
"HISCZ2MD";"The Czechoslovakian 2. Motostřelecká Divize, or 2nd Motorized Rifle Division, was part of the frontline 1st Army located on the southern frontier of the communist country. Guarding the tri-border area of Czechoslovakia, West Germany, and Austria, border guards form an integral part of this Warsaw Pact battlegroup. In case of war, the formation would have been one of the more capable units of the ČSLA, though it would rely heavily on territorial battalions to shore up any enemy breakthrough or flanking attempts. \n\nAs a mechanized division, the 2. Motostřelecká Divize fields not only plentiful OT-64 APCs, but also lavishly equipped with modernized T-55AM2 tanks, including the ATGM-wielding AM2B variant, while also being in the process of upgrading its tank regiment to the capable T-72M1. Older T-54Bs round out the battlegroup’s armor force, which will fight side-by-side with regular Motostřelci and reservists, larger Pohraničníci border guards featuring the Mountaineer trait, and various infantry scouts.  Several potent units can be deployed from the division’s arsenal, such as the R-330T Taran MT-LB-based SIGINT vehicle, the light M-46 130mm howitzers and RM-70 Cluster-equipped multiple rocket launchers, sourced from army corps detachments. The older SU-7BKL “bomb truck” ground attack aircraft will be covered by more modern Su-22M4, MiG-21MA, and MiG-23MLA as air superiority fighters."
"HISCZ303TD";"The Czechoslovakian 303. Tanková Divize, or 303rd Tank Division, was planned to be activated during war in a rear-area home defense role. The division’s cadre would come from training personnel, rounded out by reservists and territorial militia, with equipment drawn from secondary storage sites. A sprinkling of modern vehicles and weaponry would give the 303rd Tank Division a boost in combat power.\n\nThe battlegroup counts on numerous infantry, fielding weaponry of varying quality and age. They can deploy en masse, from Lidové milice to large Záložníci reservist squads in OT-65VP and OT-810/R2 half-tracks, amongst others. While an armored formation in name, the division’s large tank force mainly consists of older vehicles, including T-34/85M and SD-100 tank destroyers, backed by slightly less venerable T-54Bs, and a handful of T-72M-E2. Other vintage equipment includes KH Vz.18/47N 152mm howitzers, PTK Vz.52 85mm anti-tank guns, and the Mi-4 helicopter. One of the division’s strong points are its AA defenses, ranging from the massive PLRK Krug SAM to an array of towed AA guns, such as the large PLK KS-30 130mm. Air cover is potent, with a mix of lighter L-39 jet trainers pressed into close air support service to the ubiquitous MiG-21MF and the Su-22M4 in ground-strike roles. "
"HISDZNMXRJ";"2A26"
"HISFR11DP";"The French 11e Division Parachutiste was created in 1971 by regrouping various fast-reaction and paratrooper forces. While French divisions were generally smaller than comparable NATO formations, this Cold War battlegroup was the exception, featuring no less than seven airborne infantry regiments. It formed half of France’s quick Force Terrestre d’Intervention, deploying to Chad, Zaïre, and Lebanon. In the event of war, the 11e Division Parachutiste would rapidly deploy to the most pressing NATO sectors in West Germany.\n\nThe 11e Division Parachutiste counts on strong, fast-moving infantry, with plenty of units featuring the Airborne trait. These include veteran Chasseurs-Paras and Sapeurs-Paras, elite Legionnaires-Paras, plus supporting weapon teams and vehicles. A second wave is composed of Aeromobiles in Puma helicopters and Reservistes infantry. French materiel clearly focuses on mobility, with examples such as the VBL armored car, the light ERC-90 Sagaie wheeled tank, the recon AML-90, and the VLRA Milan. The Gazelle Celtic in anti-air configuration, Puma medium helicopters in supply and command roles, and the Puma Pirate as a gunship make up the division’s helicopter force. The Armée de l’Air provides formidable air cover, from ground-attack planes such as the Mirage 5F and Jaguar in a variety of configurations to SEAD and cluster bombers. Fighters include Mirage 2000C RDI and Mirage F1C-200, plus the advanced F1 CT variant with laser-guided bombs."
"HISFR152DI";"The French 152e Division d’Infanterie was a reserve formation based near Plateau d’Albion in southeastern France. Its Cold War mission was simple: to protect the critically important French nuclear arsenal and missile silos at Base Aérienne 200 from any prospective enemy incursion, sabotage, or air assault. Formed in 1979 as a training unit with a cadre of professional soldiers as part of the 5e Division Militaire, additional reservist units would be attached in case of conflict. This includes two Régiment d’Infanterie de Marine, or naval infantry regiments, rounded out by regular infantry, armored cavalry, and combat engineers.\n\nThe 152e Division d’Infanterie counts on Base Aérienne 200’s own defenses to boost its firepower, including heavy Commandos de l’Air security special forces, a smattering of Reserviste squads, backed by Marsouins naval infantry and the VIB APC available in a range of configurations. The AML-90 armored cars can be deployed en masse, while anti-air forces are likewise potent, from the Cerbere twin 20mm guns to the formidable Crotale SAM. Air cover is very capable, from nimble Alpha Jet Es to older Fouga Magister, with additional French Aéronavale Naval Aviation F-8P Crusader and Super Etendard fighter-bombers providing key close air support."
"HISFR5DB";"The French 5e Division Blindée fought with distinction in World War II. Afterward, the armored division remained stationed in West Germany. While France officially withdrew from NATO’s integrated command in the 1960s, its forces remained closely aligned with the military alliance. The 5e Division Blindée was a mobile tank division, with French doctrine emphasizing speed over armor. At the first sign of war, the division as part of a French vanguard, would rapidly deploy to reinforce SOUTHAG-based West Germans and Americans.\n\nThe 5e Division Blindée includes the AMX-30B2, the French main battle tank of the era, and, while lightly armored, it is fast with a powerful tank gun. One of the latest variants was the AMX-30B2 Brenus with ERA reactive armor. Mechanized infantry are available as 8-man Chasseurs squads in AMX-10P IFVs or 10-man Grenadier-Voltigeurs in VAB APCs, backed by Commandos special forces. ATGM carriers firing long-range HOT 2 missiles can be deployed as the VAB Mephisto and AMX-10 HOT. The 5e Division Blindée fields strong supporting arms, from quick recon AMX-10RC Surblindé to the advanced AMX AuF1 155mm self-propelled artillery, anti-air TRM-2000 Tarasque gun trucks, and radar-controlled AMX-13 DCA. Air assets include Mirage 5 F and Jaguar ground attack planes, while Mirage III E fighters and more modern Mirage F1C-200 contest the skies for air superiority."
"HISFR6DLB";"The French 6e Division Légère Blindée , or 6th Light Armoured Division, traced its origins to a World War I cavalry division, also seeing action in World War II. During the Cold War, the formation was reorganized several times, before becoming famous as the late-1980s armored first of the Forces d'Action Rapide, France's counter-operational maneuver corps. Due to its very light organization and arsenal, and great emphasis on battlefield mobility, the division’s ability to deploy on very short notice was unrivaled in the French Army.\n\nThe 6e Division Blindée Légère is an extremely fast battlegroup, forgoing tracked vehicles or other cumbersome units for additional speed. It can also count on a large number of Légion Etrangère infantry, the Foreign Legion, deployable with extra veterancy in regular, command, Sapeurs, ATGM, and weapon teams. They are further represented with several unique vehicles from Legion. Mo-120-RT61 120mm mortar, VAB PM-81 Legion self-propelled mortar, AMX-10RC SB Legion, and P4 Milan jeeps, amongst others. The predominance of mobility leads to an eclectic mix of units, such as the Gazelle CP command helicopter and the Berliet GBU 15 supply truck, with a particularly cutting-edge weapon being the TRF-1 155mm towed artillery gun. Recon is likewise a divisional strong suit, from Spahis recon squads to AMX-10RC Legion recon armored vehicles to the SA.330B Puma Orchidee recon helicopter."
"HISFRDdR";"The French Division du Rhin was one of the shortest-lived formations to exist at the end of the Cold War. This division consolidated several rear-area and second-echelon troops in the French First Army, including reinforcements from the 7e Division Blindée and West German territorial troops. As part of SOUTHAG, it had one key mission: to protect the transfer of multiple divisions from France to southern West Germany in case of war, defending and organizing traffic around the critical Rhine bridges.\n\nThe Division du Rhin is made up of plentiful combat engineers and their equipment, as well as supporting infantry, including Reservistes, plus a powerful umbrella of anti-air units. They are backed by Sapeurs, weapon teams, Gendarmes Mobiles - transportable in police-blue Traffic Gendarmerie or VBRG armored cars - and West German Jäger squads. Vehicles and weaponry are noticeably of older origins, from M47 Dozer and AMX-13 tanks, the AMX-13 T75 featuring the venerable SS.11 missile, to F3 Automoteur 155mm self-propelled artillery and M55 Maxson quad AA. A sprinkling of advanced units can deploy, including LRM multiple rocket launchers and several aircraft, such as Alpha Jet Es, Mirage III Es with anti-tank and SEAD payloads, Mirage 2000C RDM in air defense roles, and Mirage 5 F fighter-bombers."
"HISNL4D";"The Royal Netherlands Army’s 4e Divisie was part of the I (NL) Corps, guarding the northernmost sector of NORTHAG, including the exposed Covering Force Area near the Inner German Border. Due to political considerations, Dutch war plans saw the bulk of the Corps’ units based in the Netherlands. An optimistically planned mobilization during conflict would likely not have been as rapid as envisioned, with Dutch forces in West Germany having to fend for themselves for much longer than anticipated.\n\nThe 4e Divisie’s mainstay is the state-of-the-art Leopard 2A4, giving the mechanized infantry division a serious boost in armored firepower. Older Leopard 2A1 and Leopard 1NL variants are also available. The same AIFV series of APCs and IVFs as found in the Belgian Army, designated the YPR-765 in Landmacht service, can deploy, from the convolutedly-named PRRDR radar recon, to command, supply, cargo, and a TOW-2 equipped YPR-765-PRAT. Mechanized infantry comes as Pantserinfanterie and Genie combat engineers, with Natres reservists filling out the ranks. Recon is potent and includes Verkenners recon and Korps Commandotroepen special forces squads, the 25mm autocannon-fielding M113 C&V, and the Cheetah PRLT, which is a Dutch variant of the Gepard SPAAG. The Royal Netherlands Air Force was one of the first NATO partners to field the F-16, which is backed in the sky by the older NF-5A Freedom Fighter in a variety of roles."
"HISNLCLKA";"The Dutch Commando LegerKorpsAchtergebied, or simply CKLA, stood for Rear Area Command, a war-activated command to be created as part of the I (NL) Corps fighting in NORTHAG. It would have been used to secure the immediate rear of the main Dutch divisions close to the Inner German Border. The main component of this Landmacht formation was the 101. Infanteriebrigade, supported by the VerkBat 105 recon battalion. The infantry, mostly recently called up mobilized reservists with near-regular training and equipment levels, would safeguard strategic rear-area assets, from long-range anti-air units to heavy artillery guns.\n\nThe CKLA’s arsenal features a host of capable units, from DAF YHZ-2300 Vracht heavy supply trucks, Beveiling security troops, military police’s M113 C&V KMAR APCs, to the iconic YP-408 wheeled armored vehicle series available in a variety of configurations, including YP-408 PWCO command, YP-408 PWRDR radar recon, and YP-408 PWAT tank destroyer. Older-generation Leopard 1V main battle tanks fight side-by-side with a handful of the heavy-hitting Leopard 2A4(B). Supporting arms range from cluster-equipped M270 MLRS, modernized M114/39 155m towed guns, or self-propelled M110A2 heavy artillery. Much like its ground forces, air cover is varied, from Dutch F-16A in air defense roles, American F-16C used for close air support, NF-F5A fighter-bombers, plus F-4E and F-4G Phantoms in both air superiority and SEAD roles."
"HISPOL20PD";"The 20 ""Warszawska"" Dywizja Pancerna, or 20th “Warsaw” Tank Division, was created in 1951 in Szczecinek, being turned into a full-fledged armored formation in 1955. The division took on the traditions of the 1st Warsaw Cavalry Brigade in 1967 and, as such, received the distinguishing name ""Warszawska.” It was the sole armored division of the northernmost Polish 1st Army, directed to attack either Denmark or Hamburg in conjunction with the East German 5th Army.\n\nThe 20 ""Warszawska"" Dywizja Pancerna featured one of the few BWP-2 (Polish service name for the BMP-2) battalions in the Polish People’s Army, with the IFV bringing to battle the Piechota mechanized infantry squads. The armored spearhead of the division is formed by T-55 and T-72 tanks, including the domestically upgraded T-72M2 Wilk, further supported by the very capable, wheeled AHS WZ.77 Dana 152mm self-propelled artillery. A ground radar-equipped special forces Rozp. Specjalne (GSR) team can deploy in either Polish-made Honker jeeps or BRDM-1 armored cars. Rotorcraft are few and far between, but do include the diminutive Mi-2 in Mi-2US recon and Mi-2URP Salamandra light anti-tank helicopter with Malyutka missiles. The Polish People's Air Force, or Ludowe Lotnictwo Polskie, takes to the skies with the MiG-21 in an air defense or close air support role, backed by the Su-22M4 with either a rocket or anti-tank payload."
"HISPOL4DM";"The 4 Dywizja Zmechanizowana, or 4th Mechanized Infantry Division, was originally formed in Ukraine by Polish communist forces in 1944. After World War II, the force was integrated into the new Polish People’s Army, or Ludowe Wojsko Polskie (LWP), and later reorganized as the 4th Mechanized ""Pomeranian"" Division. During the Cold War, the formation maintained full combat readiness, and in case of war, was destined to become part of the mobilized Polish 2nd Army, to see action against NORTHAG.\n\nThe Polish 4th Mechanized Infantry Division shares many similarities with its East German cousins in terms of equipment and organization, with the first-generation T-55 main battle tank as its workhorse, and the BWP-1 (BMP-1 in Polish service) as its primary IFV. Despite the Soviet-imposed uniformity, the LWP did field numerous domestic-made weapons and vehicles. Piechota, Komandosi, and Saperzy infantry either deploy with RPG-7VM or the indigenous RPG-76 Komar. The Czechoslovakian-Polish Skot is one of the main wheeled APCs, while the Star-266 is the first choice as a truck and prime mover. The upgraded T-55AM Merida, with its highly accurate fire-control system, is another example of a successful Polish design. Furthermore, Poland developed many variants of the lighter Mi-2 helicopter, including the W-3W Sokol."
"HISPOLKD";"The Korpus Desantowy was an amalgamation of Polish forces envisioned to spearhead the invasion of the outlying Danish islands in case of war, through a combined airborne and amphibious landing. The first phase of this Polish People’s Army assault was given to a mix of highly trained paratroopers of the 6 Brygada Powietrznodesantowa, or the 6th Airborne Brigade, and full combat-readiness naval infantry from 7 Brygadę Desantowa, the 7th Sea Landing Brigade. These would be backed by a follow-up wave from the 15 Dywizja Zmechanizowan, or 15th Mechanized Infantry Division.\n\nThe Korpus Desantowy is supported by the Polish People’s Navy with heavy PTS-M Zaop tracked amphibious supply vehicles, as well as the Mi-6 Zaop helicopter, and the TOPAS R-3M command unit. Infantry is the battlegroup’s strong suit, ranging from well-armed Spadochroniarze paratroopers, Desant. Saperzy squads, to Niebieski Berety naval infantry in a host of different variants, including one fielding flamethrowers. Support vehicles include TOPAS APCs mounting a SPG-9 recoilless rifle, ASU-85 light airborne tank destroyer, self-propelled 2S1M Morski Gozdzi, and the W-3RR Procjon recon helicopter. As befits an air assault formation, helicopter support is plentiful, from Mi-24D gunships to the W-3W Sokol. Polish air cover is likewise capable, with the MiG-21 9.12 and SU-22M4 available with various payloads, including SEAD, rocket, and napalm."
"HISRDA4MD";"The East German 4. Motorisierte Schützendivision was created in the 1950s as part of the new communist Nationale Volksarmee. Stationed in Gotha and Erfurt, opposite Fulda, the well-trained and politically reliable East Germans would be heavily involved in any Warsaw Pact offensive across the Inner German Border. In wartime, the mechanized infantry formation, taking part in the first attacks on NATO territory, was to be reinforced by the NVA’s elite airborne troops, the Luftsturmregiment 40. \n\nThe 4th Motorized uses either domestic equipment or export versions of Soviet Army materiel. This means older tanks, such as the T-55, upgraded T-55AM2 and T-55AM2B with its 9M117 Bastion gun-tube-fired guided missile. Infantry is a mix of cheap and resilient Motorisierte Schützen, Panzerjäger, and Pioneer squads, deployable in trucks, BTR-50PK and SPW-70 APCs, or SPZ BMP-1 IFVs. Elite East German paratroopers provide a handful of Airborne-capable Fallschirmjäger squads and the unique and secretive Fs-Einsatzgruppe and Fs-Sprengtaucher recon units. These saboteur squads, dressed as NATO troops, can perform False Flag operations. Helicopter forces are highly capable, with the Mi-8 and Mi-24 available in a range of rocket-pod, anti-tank, or gunship variants.\nThe East German Luftstreitkräfte fields older and cheaper MiG-21Bis, bolstered by MiG-23BN strike aircraft and MiG-23MF fighter-bombers. This air force is supplemented by more modern MiG-29A and Su-22M4P SEAD aircraft."
"HISRDA7PzD";"The 7. Panzerdivision was formed in 1956 with the birth of the communist Nationale Volksarmee. Like other East German formations, this armored division was modeled along Soviet Army lines, but dependent on domestic or export-variant equipment, some of it sourced from neighboring Warsaw Pact nations. In war, the 7th Armored Division would likely attack across the Inner German Border in a southwestern direction.\n\nThe 7th Armored counts on well-trained soldiers but has to make do with older, less sophisticated weaponry. The core of the formation’s firepower is clustered around the basic T-72 “mobilization tank”, backed by the more capable T-72M and T-72M1. First-generation T-55A plus T-55AK command tanks, and SPW-40P2 Konkurs ATGM carriers complement this armored fist. Supporting infantry are limited in number, ranging from Pioneer combat engineers with flamethrowers, PKM, and automatic grenade launcher weapon teams to Motorisierte Schützen deployable in either SPW-70 APCs or BMP-1 IFVs.\nCzechoslovakian-made vehicles, including the heavy T813 supply truck and MFRW RM-70 rocket launcher, can also be deployed. Recon forces range from Aufkl.Pz. BRM-1s, Spezialaufklärer squads, and nimble Mi-2 helicopters.\nThe East German air force brings a mix of older MiG-21Bis and more modern MiG-23MF in either close air support or air defense roles. The capable Su-22M4 strike aircraft also takes to the sky."
"HISRDA9PzD";"The 9. Panzerdivision was the cream of the crop of the Nationale Volksarmee, well trained and lavishly equipped. Much like the rest of the communist East German army, the division was created at its inception in 1956. Being based in Eggesin, it was earmarked for duty in the 5th Army, which was to face NORTHAG in case of war. The armored division was not only the sole NVA formation completely outfitted with the T-72, but also the solitary user of the BMP-2 in East German service.\n\nThe 9. Panzerdivision’s tanks are all variants of the T-72, available in significant numbers, including the KPz T-72M1, the T-72MUV2, and the most recent main Soviet export variant, the T-72S. Mechanized infantry ride to battle in BMPs, such as the regular SPz BMP-1, plus a new variant equipped to fire the Konkurs ATGM, as well as the more capable but rarer SPz BMP-2, transporting a Motorisierte Schützen squad fielding the state-of-the-art RPG-27. Some other notable units include the heavy T813 supply truck, which also forms the basis of the RM-70/85 napalm-firing MLRS, the Schimmwagen MAV amphibious jeep, and the GF Shturm-S Kokon-firing tank destroyer. The East German Luftstreitkräfte provides ample ground support to the division, with a mix of Su-22M4 fighter-bombers and MiG-23 fighters."
"HISRDABerl";"The Berliner Gruppierung, or Berlin Grouping, was an amalgamated battlegroup centered on the East German 1. Motorisierte Schützendivision. Arrayed around West Berlin, this force is supported by artillery and combat engineers, border guards, military police, and special forces. In wartime, it was tasked with eliminating the NATO enclave deep behind the lines as part of Unternehmen Zentrum (Operation Center).\n\nThe Berliner Gruppiering specializes in high-intensity urban warfare and has a well-equipped logistical train, from MT-LBs to Mi-8T supply helicopters. Infantry range from Motorisierte Schützen with Strela MANPADs to KdA militia, Pionier squads with AGI incendiary rocket launchers, and elite Stasi Wachschutzen. The division contains a wide range of older equipment, from T-55A tanks to the timeless T-34/85 and light ZiS-2 57mm AT gun. Artillery is well represented, from 120mm mortars to SFL-H 2S1 122mm and D-20 152mm howitzers. Not letting any piece of equipment go to waste, the dual-purpose World War II-era ZiS-3 and M-30 towed guns get a second lease of life. Anti-air defenses are formidable with plentiful Fla-Sfl 23-4 Shilka and long-range 2K12 Kub. Air focuses on ground support aircraft fitted out with rocket and napalm payloads. These include the capable Su-22M4, MiG-21Bis light bomber, and the cheap L-39ZO trainer. Not close to the front, fighter cover is limited to MiG-23ML fighters."
"HISRDAKdA";"The Kampfgruppen der Arbeiterklasse Bezirk Erfurt, or Erfurt District’s Combat Group of the Working Class, was an East German reserve force made up of citizen soldiers and paramilitary units. This defensive formation, equipped with an arsenal of mothballed materiel, was to be used to secure the Warsaw Pact’s rear and protect vital military sites and friendly heavy corps assets such as artillery and anti-air units.\n\nK.d.A. Bezirk Erfurt calls on especially large KdA militia squads, fielding older small arms, with additional Sicherungs, Militarstreifen, and Soviet Zagradotryad military police, as well as Reservisten deployable in BTR-152 and BTR-50 APCs. The divisional logistical base is generous, including the heavy M-26 supply helicopter. Artillery is likewise well-regarded, from M-46 130mm howitzers to the super-heavy 2S7M Malka. Various MLRS systems can also unleash their devastating rocket payloads, such as the venerable heavy BM-24M, the BM-21 with its Napalm warheads, and the Cluster-equipped BM-30 Smerch. Anti-air units include the ZSU-57-2 SPAAG and long-range 9K37 Buk-M1. With much of the division’s equipment being older-generation, or even obsolete, armored forces have to make do with T-54Bs and a smattering of T-62s, PT-76s, including a recon version, and museum-worthy T-34/85M tanks. Fixed-wing air support is divided between Soviet and East German air forces, from rocket-wielding MiG-21bis to anti-tank MiG-27M, the SEAD Su-24MP, and MiG-23MF fighters."
"HISRDARug";"The Rügener Gruppierung, or Rügener Grouping, took its name from Rügen Island, on the East German Baltic Coast, the location of the main communist Volksmarine naval base. To defend this critically important site, a substantial Nationale Volksarmee garrison was in place, the Besondere Gruppierung II (Special Grouping II). In war, the formation was to be bolstered by reservists, troops in training, and allied Polish units. The amalgamated battlegroup was also to secure the nearby Sassnitz ferry port, through which much of the USSR's strategic military supply entered East Germany. \n\nThe mixed East German and Polish Rügener Gruppierung contains various mobilized detachments and formations under a single unified command. These include East German Marinepionier squads backed by Reservisten, Vopos militia, and Polish Piechota Zmech. infantry deployable in STAR-266 trucks or TOPAS-2A APCs. Supporting combat arms are plentiful, including the short-range mine-clearing SPW-50PK(MRF) MRLS, the SPW-40P recon armored car, large amphibious Schwimmwagen PTS-M tracked supply vehicle, towed PAK K-52 85mm, East German scout-engineer recon diver squads, and even elite KSK special forces. Other supporting units include the Mi-8TB helicopter and its rare Mi-14PL anti-ship variant, the Flak KS-19M2 100mm AA gun, Fasta-4 SAM, and the massive 2K11M3 Krug-M3. Air cover is likewise potent, from the nimble Polish LiM-6M to the MiG-23BN [KMGU] with its anti-personnel cluster bombs."
"HISRFA1LLD";"The West German 1. Luftlandedivision, or the 1st Air Landing Division, was raised in 1956, a year after the Bundeswehr’s founding. The initial deployment saw the formation’s use as a strategic reserve dispersed among the three main West German corps. At the tail end of the Cold War, the Bundeswehr consolidated most of the division in the Bavarian south, bolstered by the Gebirgsjägerbrigade 23 and territorial troops of the well-armed Heimatschutzbrigade 56.\n\nThe 1. Luftlandedivision contains a well-trained cadre of Airborne- and Mountaineer-traited infantry, from Forward Deployable Fallschirmjäger to Gebirgsjäger and elite Hochgebirgsjäger, backed by various helicopters and Airliftable transports. They excel at fighting in rough terrain. This expertise is extended to recon units, with large Gebirgsjäger Aufklärer and Jagdkommando troops deploying side-by-side with Fallschirmjäger B1 commandos. Vehicles range from Marder 1A1 IFVs, a rare Leopard 1A1A2, and Aufkl. Leopard 1A5 recon tank, and the reservist-manned M48A2GA2. The light Italian-made FS-M56 105mm howitzer, designed explicitly for mountainous warfare, can also be deployed, as well as the fast CL-289 recon drone and truck-mounted Unimog S404 FK-20 anti-air. Located near the Wehrtechnische Dienststelle 61, the Bundeswehr's technical center for aircraft improvement, a variety of exotic testbed planes can be used, from F-4F with laser-guided bombs, Tornado IDS in SEAD variant, the HFB-320/ECM electronic warfare aircraft, to the nimble Alpha Jet A KWS with anti-tank missiles."
"HISRFA2PzG";"The 2. Panzergrenadier-Division was one of the Bundeswehr’s founding formations in 1956. As part of the West German III Corps, the mechanized infantry division served in the northern reaches of CENTAG. Based in Kassel, it constituted a vital link between NATO’s strategic commands. In war, additional support would come from a Belgian recon regiment and RAF air cover.\n\nThe 2. Panzergrenadier-Division relies on mechanized infantry fighting in close cooperation with tanks. Some of the most modern West German armored vehicles are available to support the Panzergrenadier squads, from the Marder IFV to the Leopard 2A3 main battle tank. Airborne infantry can Forward Deploy as lightly equipped Fallschirmjäger squads, recon, and weapon teams. Belgian recon units include Eclaireurs scouts and British-made CVR(T) vehicle series, such as the Scimitar light tank, Spartan APC, and Striker ATGM carrier. Artillery and anti-air units are powerful and plentiful, including the LARS 2 MLRS, towed I-Hawk, and Gepard 1A1 SPAAGs. The skies above are protected by a mix of Luftwaffe, Belgian Air Force, and RAF Germany planes. The West Germans field Phantom F-4F and Tornado strike aircraft in various configurations, the Belgians F-16 fighters and Mirage 5BA tactical bombers, while the British provide Harrier GR.3, as well as their Tornado F.3 and GR.1 in air superiority and SEAD variants."
"HISRFA5PzD";"The Bundeswehr’s 5. Panzerdivision was assigned to III Corps, located in the north of CENTAG. As part of the founding of the new West German army in 1956, the armored division was based in Hesse. In war, the division’s panzers would have played an important role in containing Warsaw Pact forces before counterattacking the communists in the region north of Fulda.\n\nThe 5. Panzerdivision’s tank arsenal is formidable and includes not only a large contingent of older Leopard 1A1A1 and Leopard 1A5, but also the Jaguar 1 and 2 ATGM carriers, the modern Leopard 2A3, and its most heavily armored and advanced variant, the Leopard 2A4. The West German formation counts on Panzergrenadier mechanized infantry, as well as Sicherungs and Jäger squads, deployable in soft-skin vehicles, Marder IFVs, and M113A1Gs. Recon contains Alouette II helicopters and Fernspaher special forces. Artillery features both towed and self-propelled options, such as Panzermorser mortar carriers, MARS rocket artillery, and FH155-1 howitzers. The Gepard 1A1, along with the Roland 2 and 3 SAM systems, provides a deadly anti-air shield. In the skies above, the Luftwaffe fields the F-4F in anti-tank, rocket, tactical bomber, and air superiority roles. The modern Tornado IDS strike aircraft, in various close air support variants, can also be deployed, including one with the destructive anti-infantry cluster MW-1 dispenser."
"HISRFATKS";"Territorialkommando Süd, meaning Territorial Command South, covered a host of West German rear-area and reserve troops stationed in CENTAG and SOUTHAG. A handful of allied NATO units supported this division-sized battlegroup. These second-line forces would be first responders to sabotage or airborne operations, or used as a last-ditch effort to contain Warsaw Pact breakthroughs.\n\nTerritorialkommando Süd has an excellent logistical base with its MAN Kat 6x6, UH-1D and CH-53G helicopter supply units. Cheap and numerous are its infantry, from Jäger squads to Heimatschützen, Feldjäger military police, and MILAN ATGMs with their MTW M113A1G MILAN transports. NATO support comes as elite American Green Berets, French heliborne Aeromobiles squads, recon AMX-10 RC, and Gazelle helicopters. Territorialkommando Süd has to make do with West German tank reserves, chiefly the old M48A2CGA1 and A2 variants, plus Kanonenjagdpanzer. Artillery contains the Hs.30 Panzermorser and the long-range M110A2 203mm howitzer. Much more powerful is the division’s anti-air defenses, ranging from towed Flak L/70 Bofors 40mm and I-Hawk to the self-propelled Roland 2 and 3 SAMs. The divisional air cover is best described as a flying circus of older Luftwaffe aircraft, from museum-worthy GINA G.91R/3 to Alpha Jet trainers and reserve F-104Gs, with a few more capable French Mirage 2000C RDI fighters and American F-111F LGB variants in support."
"HISSO119OG";"The Soviet 119-y Odtelniy Tankoviy Polk, or 119th Independent Tank Regiment, was stationed in Bad Langensalza, East Germany. This type of second-echelon formation served as an exploitation force, projected to advance deep into NATO’s operational rear once a breakthrough had been achieved. In the case of a Fulda Gap offensive, this armored spearhead of the Soviet 8th Guards Army was to form the core of a small Operational Maneuver Group with an engineer brigade and recon regiment attached.\n\nThe battlegroup calls on the most fearsome and advanced of the Soviet main battle tanks: the heavily armored T-80UD and the earlier T-80U. The T-80BVK command tanks provide local leadership, while TO-55 flamethrower tanks and Rapira towed anti-tank guns add extra firepower. The very destructive TOS-1 Buratino short-range thermobaric rocket launcher can also deploy. The Soviet armored force might be formidable, but its supporting arms - from logistics to infantry - are limited. Infantry consists of a handful of Spetsnaz special forces and Saperi combat engineers. Artillery and anti-air units are likewise constrained, with only a few self-propelled 2S1 Gvozdika and towed 2A65 Msta-B 152mm howitzers, 2K22 Tugunska SPAAGs, and MT-LB Strela-10 SAM units. Helicopter and air forces are capable, with a good deal of Mi-24V attack helicopters backed by MiG-29 and Su-27S fighters, and Su-24M strike aircraft with various loadouts."
"HISSO157";"The Soviet 157-ya Motostrelkovaya Diviziya, or 157th Motor Rifle Division, was based in the Crimea, protecting the vitally important Black Sea Fleet bases near Sevastopol. A mobilization division with only a limited cadre of professional soldiers during peacetime, the defensive formation was first raised in 1969. As part of the Soviet Army’s 32nd Army Corps, the division’s reservists would have absorbed nearby training units, as well as Soviet Navy assets, in times of armed conflict.\n\nThe 157th fields a small force of regular Motostrelki squads, supported in significant numbers by Rezervisiti relying on older BTR-152K and BTR-40 APCs. Fielding a museum-worthy quantity of older small arms are the truck-borne Partizani squads, backed by some equally ancient IS-2M tanks taken out of mothballs. Slightly more modern armor are T-54B and T-55As, but most of the support arms stem from World War II, including BS-3 100mm anti-tank guns, D-1 152mm howitzers, BM-24M MLRS, and the super-heavy B-4M 203mm and Br-5M 280mm artillery behemoths. Naval and coastal defense units include K-1 recon helicopters, the state-of-the-art A222 Bereg 130mm self-propelled artillery, and the KSM-65 100mm towed anti-tank gun. Air support comes in the form of the older Su-15TM interceptor and the T-10K, a navalised Su-27K flown by Soviet Navy pilots."
"HISSO17TDG";"The 17-ya Gvardeyskaya Tankovaya Diviziya, or 17th Guards Tank Division, was, despite its renowned “Guard” designation, a low-readiness mobilization division based in the Ukrainian SSR. With only a skeleton crew, this second-echelon division would rapidly muster its reserve forces upon war. The 17th Guards would likely be directed into nearby Czechoslovakia, scooping up a host of army-level attachments before entering the fray. \n\nThe 17th Guards Tank Division concentrates all of the remaining early-production T-64R main battle tanks, further backed by a sizable contingent of World War II-era ISU-152K self-propelled guns and even more numerous T-10M, the ultimate specimen of the post-war Iosef Stalin-series of heavy tanks. A handful of regular Motostrelki squads are supplemented by Rezervisti and Pogranvoiska KGB border guards, including recon variants, deployed near the USSR’s internal frontier with Czechoslovakia. Several East German and Polish pieces of equipment have also found their way into this battlegroup, such as the reservist-manned ML-20 152mm howitzers, the BM-14M MRLS, the self-propelled 2S7M Malka, and the 2S4 Tyulpan super-heavy 240mm mortar, plus the ZSU-23-4M1 Shilka SPAAG. The division’s air cover is provided by the MiG-23ML and the longer-range MLA variant, with an all-out air-fleet of Su-17M4 providing close air support, including with Thermobaric and combined HE and CLU payloads. "
"HISSO25TD";"The Soviet Army’s 25-ya Tankovaya Diviziya, or the 25th Tank Division, saw the light after World War II’s conclusion, being destined for garrison duty in Soviet-occupied Germany. Based in East German Vogelsang, near the Polish border, the armored division was part of the 20th Guards Combined Army. As a powerful follow-up force, it would have been used to exploit any communist breakthrough into the North German Plains. \n\nThe 25th Tank Division, unlike any other Soviet Army formation, is not only fully equipped with state-of-the-art T-64 main battle tanks but also features four instead of three tank regiments. The unusual lack of an infantry regiment means that only a limited number of Motostrelki and Saperi squads will be available. The battlegroup’s tank force is formidable, with a whole arsenal of T-64B, B1, and older T-64A Obr. 83, with variants differing in fire control systems, ERA, armor, or the ability to fire anti-tank guided missiles. The T-64B1 Razv. can be deployed as a potent recon tank, with the Schmel-1 UAV watching from the sky above. Some heavy self-propelled artillery, courtesy of the 34th Artillery Division, can deploy, including the long-range 2S5 Giatsint-S and the brand-new 2S19 Msta-S."
"HISSO27G";"The 27-ya Gvardeyskaya Motostrelkovaya Diviziya, or the 27th Guards Motor Rifle Division, was earmarked in 1989 to be the next-generation Soviet Army formation. Designated a testbed for the “Division ‘90” concept, a number of cutting-edge weaponry was introduced by the Group of Soviet Forces Germany. However, looming conflict in Europe limited the round of experimentation to this single modernized combined-arms division.\n\nThe 27th Guards has access to some of the latest hardware to be deployed in the Soviet Army. Motostrelki and Saperi squads feature new camouflage uniforms, RPG-26 and RPG-27 rocket launchers, while Spetsrazvedka recon squads, Otdelenie Podderzhki tank hunters, and Konkurs-M ATGM teams can also deploy. The state-of-the-art BMP-3 is available as an IFV, supported by T-80BV armor. The wheeled BRDM-2 Konkurs-M and the hard-hitting but short-range towed 2A45M Sprut-B provide additional anti-tank firepower. Artillery is modern, from the 2S12 120mm mortar to the wheeled 2S23 Nona-SVK, towed 2A36 Giatsint-B 152mm howitzer, and precision-guided artillery shells of the upgraded 2S3M1 Akatsiya. Anti-air is likewise potent, including the Strela-10M3 and 9K330 Tor systems. The Soviet Air Forces deploy the Su-17M4 attack aircraft, MiG-23MLD and MiG-29 fighters, and the next-generation close-support plane, the T-8M, bristling with Vikhr anti-tank missiles."
"HISSO2G";"The Soviet 2-ya Tamanskaya Gvardeyskaya Motostrelkovaya Diviziya, or 2nd Guards Tamanskaya Motorized Rifle Division, was a prestigious formation protecting the capital of the USSR. Beginning its life as the 127th Rifle Division in 1940, the unit saw extensive action during the Great Patriotic War, becoming one of the most famous and decorated formations in the Red Army, even attaining the Guards and Tamanskaya honorifics. In the late Cold War, the Moscow-based division was highly trained and lavishly equipped. Officers were handpicked for their loyalty, as this formation was envisioned not only to guard against foreign attacks but also domestic threats, including rebellions. \n\nThe 2nd Guards can call upon some of the latest models of tanks and air superiority fighters available to the Soviet Army, with its Gvardeitsy infantry squads fielding their own type of uniform and small arms. As a mechanized infantry division, it follows the standard communist template of motorized Motostrelki squads backed by a sizable main battle tank contingent. Armor includes the T-72A Obr. 83 main battle tank and a handful of the state-of-the-art T-80U obr. 1989 with Kontakt-5 ERA. Other special units include SIGINT-capable R-330 RAMA trucks, recon Razv BTR-80 APCs, while patrolling the capital’s skies are the ground-strike MiG-23P aircraft, Su-15TM interceptors, and advanced MiG-29 9.13 fighters."
"HISSO31TD";"The Soviet 31-ya Tankovaya Diviziya, or the 31st Tank Division, was the direct successor to the World War II-era 31st Tank Corps of the Red Army, a formation that ended the war in Czechoslovakia. Reorganized and reformed, the division was stationed in nearby Hungary before taking part in the Warsaw Pact’s intervention during the Prague Spring of 1968. Afterwards, the tank division remained in eastern Czechoslovakia for the duration of the Cold War, subordinated to the Soviet Central Group of Forces. \n\nThe 31st Tank Division can deploy a wide array of capable Soviet Army units, from the massive Mi-22 command helicopter to a large number of the sprawling T-72 tank family, with the T-72A obr. 79 being the mainstay, to the 9A51 Prima, a heavier variant of the Grad-based MRLS system. The battlegroup can also count on a large contingent of Czechoslovakian troops to bolster its ranks in the field, including Střelci infantry and ATGM weapon teams, RM Vz.51 130mm MLRS, H D-30 122mm howitzers, and self-propelled Ještěrka twin 30mm SPAAG. A curious recon unit is the BMAN, a rocket-wielding spotting vehicle featuring one of the few advanced Electro-Optical Dazzler systems in Soviet service."
"HISSO35VDV";"The 35-ya Gvardeyskaya Desantno-Shturmovaya Brigada, or the 35th Guards Air Assault Brigade, traced its origins to the late 1940s. Part of the VDV (Soviet Airborne Forces), it was trained and specifically equipped for air assaults. Briefly deployed to Afghanistan, the formation was transferred to East Germany, where it became the 35th Guards Air Assault Brigade. In wartime, the VDV would attack key strategic points or conduct operations behind enemy lines.\n\nThe 35th Guards Air Assault features a mix of trained Desantniki, veteran Afgantsy, and Spetsnaz squads with Forward Deployment and follow-up infantry deploying in Mi-2 and Mi-8T helicopters. Uniquely for an air assault formation, it is highly mechanized, relying on the heavily armed but lightly armored BMD and BRT-series, also sporting the Airborne trait. These include the BMD-1 and -2, anti-tank BRT-RD Robot, anti-air BTR-D Skrezhet, and recon 1V119 Reostat. Tanks are non-existent, with most of the supporting arms made up of light and specialized units, ranging from 2B9 Vasilek automatic mortar and self-propelled 2S9 Nona, to the BM-21V Grad-V MRLS, towed ZU-23-2 23mm, and D-44 85mm anti-tank guns. Heliborne support is substantial, from the recon Mi-24K to the advanced but rare Ka-50 attack helicopter. Air cover comprises the MiG-27 bomber in various loadouts, the MiG-25BM SEAD and MiG-25RBF bombers, and the MiG-23ML and MiG-29 fighters."
"HISSO39G";"The Soviet 39-ya Gvardeyskaya Motostrelkovaya Diviziya, or the 39th Guards Motorized Rifle Division, began its illustrious career in Stalingrad’s Red October steelworks in 1942, ending victorious at Berlin’s Brandenburg Gate in 1945. A permanent readiness division based in East Germany, it was part of the Soviet 8th Guards Army. In war, this well-equipped division was to spearhead the Warsaw Pact’s offensive through the Fulda Gap.\n\nAs a motorized rifle division, the 39th Guards was to break through heavily defended sectors during combined-arms operations. Regular Motorstrelki infantry and Saperi assault squads deploy with a variety of weapons and vehicles, including RPG-7V and RPG-22 anti-tank rockets, short-range Metis ATGMs, wheeled BTR-60s, or tracked BMP-1 and BMP-2 IFVs. A sizable number of T-80B and T-80BV provide armored back-up, further supported by long-range MT-LB Shturm-S ATGM carriers. Radzveka scouts, deploying alongside East German Grenzer border troops and recon helicopters, provide battlefield intel. The 2S3M Akatsiya and BM-27 Uragan MLRS, plus the 9K33M3 OSA-AKM and 2K12 Kub SAM systems, are some of the self-propelled artillery and anti-air units available. Helicopter support is powerful with Mi-8 and well-armed Mi-24 gunships. Air cover is likewise potent, from the slow-flying but armored Su-25 to Su-24 strike aircraft, East German Su-22M4 and MiG-23MF tactical bombers, MiG-27K equipped with laser-guided bombs, and MiG-23MLD and Su-27S fighters."
"HISSO56VDV";"The Soviet 56-ya Otdel’naya Gvardeyskaya Desantno-Shturmovaya Brigada, or 56th Separate Guards Air Assault Brigade, had a history that was closely tied to the Soviet-Afghan War of the 1980s. The particular VDV battlegroup was created from several independent units, and only two months after its inception, it took part in the initial invasion of Afghanistan. In time, the Soviet brigade became closer to a mechanized infantry formation, using BMP-2s and additional firepower of T-62 tanks. With conflict in Europe on the horizon, the experienced 56th Separate Guards Air Assault Brigade was transferred to East Germany, to be an integral part of the Warsaw Pact’s offensive plans against NATO.\n\nThe 56th Separate Guards Air Assault Brigade fields some of the most battle-hardened airborne veterans of the Soviet Army, backed by a series of unique battlefield-modified vehicles. These range from Spetsnaz GRU (Stinger) special forces equipped with looted NATO weapons to lightly armed Okhrana squads with RPO Rys and RPG-16 rocket launchers. Improvised units include the ZSU-23-4M2 (PSNR), an anti-air SPAAG converted for ground surveillance, the LuAZ amphibious jeeps, a variety of wheeled BTR-70 and tracked GM-TU vehicles, and the super-heavy towed M-240 mortar. In the skies above, the Mi-8PPA jamming helicopter and Mi-24P gunships are joined by the MiG-27, which provides potent anti-tank air support."
"HISSO6GOB";"The Soviet 6-ya Gvardeyskaya Motostrelkovaya Brigada, or 6th Guards Separate Motor Rifle Brigade, was the Warsaw Pact counterpart to the NATO garrisons stationed in West Berlin. Formed after the Berlin Crisis of 1962, it protected the communist East Berlin, providing military police and ceremonial troops. However, in times of conflict, reinforced for the Warsaw Pact’s offensive Unternehmen Zentrum plans, the formation would spearhead the assault on the city from within its tight urban confines.\n\nThe 6th Guards battlegroup counts on a host of experienced infantry, mostly Soviet Motostrelki and Saperi squads, Komendatura military police, backed by East German Vopos militia and Motorisierte Schützen in BMPs. Several special forces and paratrooper squads are also available, including East German Luftsturm-Jäger squads transportable in armed Mi-2 and Mi-8 helicopters, and the KGB’s elite Spetsgruppa “A” saboteur squads with their False Flag trait and civilian attire. The capable T-64 tanks, including the upgraded T-64B variant, provide some much-needed armor support, while artillery forces can deploy the long-range 2S5 Giantsint-S and powerful BM-27 Urugan MRLS. This far from the front, patrolling the skies against enemy intruders and bombers rests on the shoulders of the Soviet Air Defence Forces’ long-range MiG-31M interceptor. Other aircraft include the L-39ZO trainer, which also doubles up as a light bomber. "
"HISSO76VDV";"The Soviet 76-ya Gvardiyska Vozdushno-Desantnaya Diviziya, or 76th Guards Airborne Division, traced its lineage back to the Red Army’s 157th Rifle Division of World War II. The parent division fought with distinction in various epic battles, from Stalingrad to Kursk, Operation Bagration, and the Battle of Berlin. After the war, it was reformed as a Soviet airborne division, part of the VDV, specifically equipped for air assault missions. With World War III looming in Europe, the well-trained division would have had the unenviable task of destroying the French nuclear weapons in a high-risk Warsaw Pact mission deep in enemy territory. \n\nThe 76th Guards Airborne Division counts on a significant proportion of its troops going to battle in light but highly advanced equipment, including the state-of-the-art BMD-3 armored vehicle in both tank and recon roles. Earlier generations of the BMD are also available, such as the BTR-D, ready to transport Desantniki, Desant. Sapery and large Desant. Usilennie VDV infantry squads. Other specialized units featured are the Desant. Gaz-66B SNAB supply truck, LuAZ Korrektirovschik artillery command unit, LuAZ 2F62 Zenitchik AA units, and Schmel-1 UAV for remote aerial recon. The Soviet Air Forces provide long-range aviation support in the form of newly equipped SU-24M, including one variant with powerful thermobaric bombs, and the fast MiG-31 air defense fighter."
"HISSO79G";"The Soviet 79-ya Gvardeyskaya Tankovaya Diviziya, or the 79th Guards Tank Division, was forged in the flames of Stalingrad, before fighting its way through the Crimea, Poland, East Prussia, and ultimately Berlin. Remaining in East Germany, the unit was reorganized as a tank division in 1965. A high-readiness formation, the 79th was one of the best-equipped and trained in the Group of Soviet Forces in Germany. In case of conflict, as part of the 8th Guards Army, it was planned to exploit any breakthrough in the Fulda Gap.\n\nThe 79th Guards calls on the mobility and firepower of the latest series of Soviet main battle tanks. As such, it fields the T-80BV with reactive armor, including a distinct variant with a supercharged engine, backed by earlier T-80Bs. Limited Motostrelki squads in wheeled APCs, BMP-1s, or BMP-2s IFVs provide infantry support. Recon forces include Spetznas G.R.U. and Razdvedka scout squads deployable in BMP-2s or rocket-armed helicopters. Self-propelled anti-air defenses are heavily employed, ranging from Strela-10M and heavy long-range Buk-M1 to state-of-the-art 2K22 Tunguska SPAAGs. The Soviet Air Forces are out for war, flying everything from the Su-25 in a variety of close-air support loadouts, to Su-24M tactical bombers, MiG-27K SEAD planes, and MiG-23ML and MiG-29 fighters for air superiority missions."
"HISSOV1G";"The Soviet 1-ya Gvardeyskaya Proletarskaya Motostrelkovaya Diviziya, or the 1st Guards Proletarian Motorized Infantry Division, was one of the longest-serving formations of the Soviet Army.\nFirst formed in 1926 from various independent and training battalions in the Moscow region, it was destroyed and reformed at least once during World War II.\nIt ended in 1945 near Königsberg, East Prussia, having attained the esteemed Guards status.\n\nBased in the Kaliningrad Oblast as part of the Baltic Military District, the reduced combat-ready division’s role would have been to be mobilized quickly and used as a second echelon of any strategic war offensive.\nRushed to the front, and reinforced by several anti-tank formations, the division would have arrived in the East German Magdeburg area just in time to repel NATO’s surprise counter-attack.\n\n  "
"HISSPA1DM";"The Spanish División Mecanizada «Brunete» n.º 1, or Armoured Division No. 1 ""Brunete"", was created by the Franco regime in 1943, and named after an important Nationalist-won battle of the Spanish Civil War. When a newly democratic Spain joined NATO in 1982, the tank division was considered one of the best-armed of the Ejército de Tierra. In case of hostilities, it was to quickly reinforce SOUTHAG in West Germany. \n\nThe Armoured Division No. 1 ""Brunete"" is a small formation with only two brigades, fielding a mix of domestic, French, and American equipment. The main battle tank is a Spanish AMX-30 variant with a light coaxial machine gun. Infantry come as Fusileros or Zapadores squads, deployable in Pegaso trucks, Santana PA jeeps, tracked TOA (M113), or the 6x6 wheeled BMR APC family. Part of the Brigada de Caballería “Jarama” I regiment is attached, bringing excellent recon forces, from Francotiradores snipers to wheeled VEC-25 and VEC-90 armored vehicles, plus the recon AMX-30EMI tank. Anti-air includes AMX-30RE SPAAG, Apside Toledo towed SAMs, and various gun platforms. The Ejército del Aire provides excellent air support with three types of aircraft: the C.12 (American F-4C) used in a ground attack role; the C.14A (French Mirage F1) as a bomber and fighter; and the C.15 (American F-18) in AT or air defense roles."
"HISSPA2DM";"The Spanish División Mecanizada «Guzmán el Bueno» n.º 2, or Mechanised Division No.2 ""Guzmán el Bueno"", was one of the largest formations in the Spanish Army during the closing years of the Cold War. Based in southern Andalucia and named after a Spanish noble and hero during medieval times, it was envisioned to either deploy rapidly against potentially belligerent African nations or support NATO allies if conflict arose in West Germany. Mechanized by name, but motorized by nature, the battlegroup would be further reinforced by a variety of corps assets upon its call to action. \n\nThe ""Guzmán el Bueno"" relies on smaller, infantry squads transported in a wide array of BMR APC variants, further supported by the light M47E2 and the more capable M48A5E2 tanks. Guerilleros recon special forces can deploy ahead of the main infantry, consisting of Fusileros and Zapadores squads. Additional corps assets include units such as the World War II-vintage Cañón 122/45 (Ruso .31), the L-10D3 300mm MLRS, Teleoka Electronic Warfare ground vehicles, and heavy C-3464 logistic trucks. UH-1H Mamee helicopter gunships provide local air cover, while the Ejército del Aire operates export variants of the Mirage III (C.11 in Spanish service) and Mirage F1 (C.14) in a variety of close air support and air defense roles."
"HISUK1AD";"The British 1st Armoured Division’s insignia was a testament to its tapestried military history, combining the rhinoceros of its World War II namesake and the red-bordered triangle of the 1st Division. Permanently stationed near the Inner German Border, the late Cold War-era “heavy” 1st Armoured Division was part of the British Army of the Rhine. The NORTHAG-based tank and anti-tank forces, together with airborne reserves from the British Isles, would contain and then counter any Warsaw Pact offensive.\n\nThe 1st Armoured Division fields an extensive arsenal of British armored vehicles, from FV432 Command to Warrior IFVs, bringing Armoured Rifles and Gun Group mechanized infantry squads. Several Forward Deployed-capable Terriers Paras and weapon teams are also available. Tank forces include the modern Challenger I Mk.2 and Mk.3, backed by older Chieftain Mk.9 and Mk. 11s. Long-range ATGM carriers, the FV438 Swingfire and FV102 Striker, can also be fielded. FV101 Scorpion and the FV721 Fox, supported by Scout, Sniper, and elite 4-man SAS Patrol squads, make up its recon forces. Supporting arms include the self-propelled FV432 Mortar and FV433 Abbot 105mm howitzer and the anti-air Tracked Rapier. RAF Germany brings close air support Harriers and Jaguar GR.1s, as well as Tornado F.3 air defense and Tornado GR.1 strike aircraft."
"HISUK2ID";"The British 2nd Infantry Division had a checkered past, reformed and reconstituted various times throughout its almost two hundred years of existence. In 1983, a reorganization incorporated a light airmobile component. While assigned to the British Army on the Rhine, the 2nd Infantry Division was actually based in the United Kingdom. Earmarked for immediate deployment in case of conflict, the formation would reinforce NORTHAG and bolster the British I Corps as quickly as possible.\n\nThe 2nd Infantry Division favors mobility over armor. Infantry is a strong point, from rapid Airmobile troops and Airmobile Pioneers to numerous territorial reservist Terrier squads and weapon teams. Elite SAS commandos fielding AT-4 rocket launchers and Stinger AA missiles can wreak havoc behind enemy lines, while Motorized Airmobiles in Saxon APCs provide additional ground support, as do a few Armoured Rifles squads in Warrior IFVs.\n\nA handful of Challenger I tanks, seconded from strategic reserves, are available. The only self-propelled artillery piece is the M107A2 175mm gun. Anti-air defenses range from Blowpipe and Javelin MANPAD teams to towed and Tracked Rapier units.\nGazelle and Lynx in various payload loadouts provide treetop-skimming helicopter support, while RAF Harrier and Jaguar in ground attack roles, Phantom F.3 fighters, and Tornado GR.1 strike aircraft protect the skies above."
"HISUK4AD";"The 4th Armoured Division boasted an illustrious military career, having taken part in notable conflicts ranging from the Battle of Waterloo to the Boer Wars, World Wars I and II. In the late 1970s, after a series of convoluted reorganizations, the 4th Armoured Division was designated a NORTHAG frontline formation in West Germany, as part of the British Army of the Rhine.\n\nThe 4th Armoured Division forms a missing link in the British Army of the late 1980s, in effect a mechanized infantry division fielding older armored equipment. Only second-generation Chieftain main battle tanks, including Mk. 6/2 and Mk.11 variants, are available. Likewise, the formation’s plentiful Assault Pioneers, Rifles, and Motorised Rifles squads ride to battle in softskins, FV432 armored vehicles, or light but fast Saxons APCs. The FV432 is further employed in command, cargo, anti-air SCAT, MILAN, and Wombat versions. Notable units include the venerable AEC Militant Mk.3 heavy supply truck, demolition charges-firing Centurion Mk.5 AVRE ROMOR courtesy of the Royal Engineer Armoured Squadron, radar-equipped Lynx AH.7 Chancellor and rocket-firing Gazelle AH.1 helicopters. The Royal Air Force deploys Jaguars and Phantoms with various loadouts, including the Jaguar GR.1A with HE bombs and overwing air-to-air missiles, and Phantom FGR.2 fighter-bombers with HE and Cluster payloads."
"HISUKBerl";"Berlin Command was composed of the various Allied garrisons present in the Cold War’s iconic West Berlin. The U.S. Berlin Brigade, the British Berlin Infantry Brigade, and the French Forces Françaises à Berlin were to provide military deterrence. Encircled on all sides, the multinational Berlin Command was hopelessly outnumbered and outgunned. Still, these local NATO forces, specialized in urban combat, aimed to make any Warsaw Pact attack on the city an extremely costly affair.\n\nBerlin Command calls on a wide array of military police, infantry, assault troops, and combat engineers. Forces range from American elite PSSE-B recon squads to British ad-hoc RAF Rifles. The FV432 Rarden, with its 30mm autocannon, serves as a repurposed fire support vehicle. The French field the light 53T2 20mm for local AA, and the towed American M198 howitzer provides field artillery. Treaty-bound, the West Germans could only deploy police forces, such as SEK assault squads and Fr. Polizei-Reserve. Heavier armor includes the American M728 CEV and M1IP Abrams, the British Chieftain Mk.10, with its striking urban camouflage, and French AMX-13/90 and AMX-30Bs. Air assets are as varied as the ground units, including smuggled-in RAF Harrier jump jets and state-of-the-art F-117A Nighthawk stealth bombers with LGB capability. The large, high-speed French Mirage IV conducts SEAD and carpet-bombing missions."
"HISUKHDR";"The United Kingdom’s Home Defence Region London covered the British Army and Territorial units assigned to London during the Cold War. Acting as a capital garrison of sorts, it contained a hodgepodge of defensive units, with the nucleus formed by the Guards battalions of the 56th (London) Infantry Brigade. The formation was further backed by various reservist regiments, including detachments engaged in Northern Ireland, War Materiel Reserve, ceremonial artillery, training units, and even elite SAS counter-terror squads. \n\nThe Home Defence Region London deploys a wide-ranging mix of personnel and equipment, from Guards squads in their redcoats and bearskins, airborne Territorial troops, to Rifles Patrol sections redeploying from Northern Ireland, and grey-clad SAS special forces. The FV1613 Humber armored car is available in great numbers and in various configurations, supported by Centurion Mk.13 tanks, heavy Chinook HC.1B helicopters, Bedford TM supply trucks, World War II-era QF 25-pdr 88mm artillery, L5 105mm guns, to several prototypes of the state-of-the-art AS.90 155mm self-propelled gun. Anti-air and air cover is formidable, from the modern Starstreak LML to the heavy Bloodhound Mk.2 SAM. A  handful of A.109A helicopters captured from the Argentinians during the Falklands War see renewed service, together with ancient Canberra bombers, Hawk T.1A trainers, Phantom FGR.2 in air defense roles, and Harrier GR.5 attack aircraft."
"HISUKMNAD";"NATO’s MultiNational Airborne Division, or MNAD, was a late Cold War suggestion for a NORTHAG quick reaction force that never advanced beyond its proposal on paper. The limited strategic reserves of each of the national Corps were considered a risk in case of a communist offensive. With World War III on the horizon, the MNAD would see a fast-tracked revival, combining a variety of light units of the Belgian, Dutch, and West German detachments under unified British command. \n\nThe flexible MNAD relies on the elite fighting forces of the British 5 Airborne Brigade, the West German 27. Luftlandebrigade, and the Belgian Para-Commando Regiment. Paratrooper squads, from West German Fs.-Jäger to British Paras and Belgian Para-Commando wield the Airborne and Shock traits and some of their respective armies’ best small arms. Other renowned infantry featured are the famous Ghurkas and the Dutch Mariniers naval infantry. Battlefield mobility is a premium, which results in almost non-existent armor, but plenty of Airlift-capable units. These include the ATMP vehicles, L16 81mm mortar with Cluster munition, Kraka with TOWs, West German Wiesel tankettes, and even the rapid LSV M2HB buggy. Its helicopter force is powerful from Scout AH.1 Helarm, Agusta A109BA HTPT, to large CH-53G and Chinook HC.1 transports. Air is likewise well supplied with Buccaneer bombers, Mirage 5BA fighter-bombers, and F-16A air superiority fighters."
"HISUS101AB";"The renowned U.S. 101st Airborne Division (Air Assault) was first raised in World War II as a paratrooper formation, jumping famously into combat during D-Day, Market Garden, and seeing action during the Battle of the Bulge. The 101st Airborne also took part in the Vietnam War, followed by a deep reorganization that resulted in an airmobile division with close integration of helicopters and air assault-capable infantry. The late Cold War saw only limited deployment of the “Screaming Eagles”, even as part of the US Army’s quick reaction force, the XVIII Airborne Corps.\n\nThe 101st Airborne is organized as a light infantry division, but with levels of training and standards above regular U.S. Army formations, as well as substantially more helicopters, including the 160th Special Operations Aviation Regiment (Airborne), the U.S. special forces’ helicopter wing. A handful of M11P Abrams tanks will come courtesy of the 194th Armored Brigade. The light combat formation fields a wide range of specialized equipment, from Aero-Rifles squads, Green Berets (ODA), elite Delta operators, to the quirky 6x6 Gama Goat and M274 Mule transports. Air support includes the heavily armed MH-47D Chinook, nimble AH-6H Little Bird, MH-60A DAPs, and AH-64A Apache ATAS helicopters, as well as EF-11A Raven Electronic Warfare planes and F-15C Eagles for air superiority."
"HISUS11ACR";"The U.S. 11th Armored Cavalry Regiment “Blackhorse” was CENTAG’s tripwire, a screening force situated directly on the Inner German Border. With the outbreak of war, the regiment’s squadrons were to be reinforced with a few West German and American battalions, intent on holding back the Warsaw Pact for as long as possible. Manning outposts such as the famous OP Alpha, U.S. 11th Armored Cavalry Regiment “Blackhorse’s” wartime mission near the Fulda Gap would be near-sacrificial, with life expectancy counted in hours.\n\nThe 11th Armored Cavalry Regiment’s recon units are top-notch, from LRS special forces and M1025 Humvee AGL to West German radar-equipped Green Archer and light Bundesgrenzschutz border guards. One of the most impressive is the M1A1 ACAV recon tank. Much like its logistical train and supporting arms, the regiment’s mechanized infantry is expensive to deploy but includes Engineers and Dismounted Troopers. The cavalry’s armor is well represented, with M1A1 Abrams bringing their heavy tank guns to bear. Attack helicopters can likewise be deployed cheaply but are limited to the older AH-1F Cobra and the AH-1F C-Nite with TOW-2 missiles. Flying top cover is the F-16 Fighting Falcon in various loadouts, including the F-16CG with laser-guided bombs, while the fearsome A-10 Thunderbolt provides devastating close air support. "
"HISUS1CAV";"The U.S. 1st Cavalry Division was formed in 1921 as a horse cavalry unit and saw action in the Pacific Theatre during World War II, and later in the Korean War.\nRemaining in East Asia, the formation was reformed into an air assault division and saw further service in Vietnam, including famously at the Battle of Ia Drang. In the late 1980s, the 1st Cavalry Division was based in the continental United States as a test-bed formation.\n\nThe division was to be ferried to a war-engulfed Europe as part of REFORGER, using local POMCUS depots with ready-to-roll equipment.\nThe formation’s hurried deployment in NATO’s Magdeburg Counterstrike, without its usual National Guard brigade, would see the division take temporary command of the British 4th Armoured Brigade to bolster its battlefield presence.\n\n  "
"HISUS24ID";"Formed during World War II to fight in the Pacific, the U.S. 24th Infantry Division (Mechanized) saw further action in the Korean War. Shuffled between Europe and the United States during the Cold War, the mechanized formation was reactivated in the late ‘70s. Not earmarked as a REFORGER division, deployment to Europe for this battlegroup in case of war would have been a lengthy affair.\n\nA mechanized division with some of the latest equipment available, the reservist National Guard will make up about a third of the 24th Infantry Division’s strength. Less experienced, fielding older small arms, vehicles, and weaponry, these American units with the Reservist traits are still capable enough when used in numbers. National Guard units include infantry squads either with Dragon or LAW anti-tank weapons in M2 Bradleys, M60 machine gun and Stinger MANPAD weapon teams, 105mm-equipped M1 Abrams, I-Tow mounted on jeeps, M109A2 self-propelled howitzers, and even A-64A Apache attack helicopters. Regular units featured are the tracked M548A2 supply, M1IP Abrams, as well as large Military Police combat squads. Protecting the skies above, one of the most advanced jet fighters flies air cover in two variants: the F-15C Eagle air superiority fighter and the F-15E Strike Eagle with laser-guided bombs."
"HISUS35ID";"The U.S. 35th Infantry Division (Mechanized) could count on a long service record, having seen action in World War I and II. The distinctive blue cross-in-circle insignia of the formation gave rise to the “Santa Fe Division” nickname. Re-established as a mechanized infantry division in the early 1980s, with plentiful armored battalions, it acted as the missing link between the U.S. Army’s mechanized and tank divisions. The formation’s core fighting forces were further supplemented by Kansas, Missouri, Nebraska, Colorado, and Kentucky National Guard units.\n\nThe 35th Infantry Division is a true National Guard formation, with many of its N.G. units featuring the Reservist trait, from infantry to vehicles. Quite a few of the division’s weapons are old enough to have seen action during the Vietnam War. These include the small arms fielded by Rifles and Engineer squads, as well as the M60A1 main battle tank in a multitude of variants, such as the improved RISE, ERA reactive armor, and an ACAV recon version. Support includes the military police M1025 Humvee MP, the heavy M813A1 supply truck, as well as the UH-1M Gunship and the slow-moving A-37B Dragonfly available in recon and close air support variants. A special unit is the experimental XM1058 US-Roland SAM, providing air cover side-by-side with the venerable M42A1 Duster SPAAG."
"HISUS3AD";"The U.S. 3rd Armored Division “Spearhead” counted on a distinguished World War II career, seeing combat from Normandy all the way to VE-Day in Germany. Reactivated in the mid-1950s, one of its most famous soldiers was Elvis Presley, serving with the formation in West Germany. Part of CENTAG, the division was headquartered in and around Frankfurt. In times of conflict, as the V Corps’ heavy tank force, the 3rd Armored Division would deploy rapidly to the front, countering any Warsaw Pact incursion through the Fulda Gap.\n\nThe 3rd Armored Division relies on its tank and anti-tank units to dominate the battlefield, fielding not only the advanced M1A1 Abrams but also the M1A1(HA), one of NATO’s most heavily armored tanks. The long-range TOW-2 ATGM is present, either as part of the M901A1 ITV or as a dismounted weapon team. While infantry can only deploy as half-sized fireteams, they come in the capable Bradley IFV.
