Air power is another strong point: the AH-64A Apache is a potent attack helicopter, while the F-111E and F-4E Phantom II are available in various close-air support loadouts. Air superiority can be handsomely achieved with the state-of-the-art F-15C. "
"HISUS6LID";"The U.S. 6th Infantry Division (Light) saw action in World War II before going dormant during most of the Cold War. Reactivation in 1986 saw it designated the U.S. Army’s primary Arctic Warfare division, tasked with the defense of Alaska, including key American military bases. If the far-flung Aleutian Islands were to come under attack, the division was also envisioned to take the fight across the “Ice Curtain” into the Soviet Far East. Limited in armored vehicles, the 6th Infantry Division combined various infantry, paratrooper, Navy, Air Force, and National Guard units.\n\nThe 6th Infantry Division’s core is made up of Light Rifles and Airborne Rifles squads with a variety of loadouts. Other U.S. Army equipment includes the heavy-lift CH-54B Tarhe helicopters, M119 105mm howitzers, and Vietnam War-era AH-1S Cobras. The National Guard is represented by Alaskan Scouts, the N.G. M48A5 ACAV recon tank, and the A-7D Corsair II attack aircraft. The U.S. Air Force, protecting its vital bases in the region, not only provides the recon OA-10A Thunderbolt but also USAF Security infantry squads with Peacekeeper wheeled APCs. In the same vein, the U.S. Navy fields the A-6E Intruder and EA-6B Prowler, plus USMC Security guarding naval facilities with Dragon 300 APCs, while the renowned Navy Seals provide special forces back-up."
"HISUS82AB";"The illustrious U.S. 82nd Airborne Division cemented its warfighting reputation with several World War II combat jumps, including the famous drops on D-Day, as well as action during Market Garden and the Battle of the Bulge. Post-war, the paratroopers formed part of the XVIII Airborne Corps’ strategic reserve and deployed to the Dominican Republic, Vietnam, and, later, Grenada in 1983. As a quick reaction force, the airborne formation would move rapidly from the continental United States to West Germany in case of hostilities.\n\nThe 82nd Airborne Division will be able to Forward Deploy most of its infantry, crew-served weapons, and vehicles, giving it a significant advantage early on in battle. Highly mobile units are the division’s hallmark, from CH-47C supply helicopters to AB M1025 TOW units, Airborne squads with AT-4s, wheeled armored reconnaissance M1047, and the M551 TTS Sheridan tank. Anti-air units include AA M998 Avengers and towed M167 Vulcan 20mm. Helicopter support is prominent, from the Zuni rocket-equipped AH-1 Heavy Hog and anti-air AH-1 ATAS to the nimble AH-6 Little Bird and modern AH-64A Apache. Air support encompasses the A-10A Thunderbolt, the potent F-15C and F-4E Phantom II in air defense roles, backed by F-16C and F-111F tactical bombers."
"HISUS8ID";"The U.S. 8th Infantry Division (Mechanized) saw extensive action in Europe during World War II, including taking part in the infamous Battle of Hürtgen Forest in late 1944. Reactivated in the mid-50s, the formation was headquartered in Bad Kreuznach, with subordinate brigades scattered west of Frankfurt. In the event of war, the division would have deployed either to protect Frankfurt or to join V Corps’ counterattacks against the invading Warsaw Pact.\n\nThe 8th Infantry Division counts on the excellent Mechanized Infantry in their M113 APCs, short-range Dragon ATGM-equipped soldiers, Aero Rifles with their UH-60A Black Hawk helicopter transports, and Ranger squads. Other infantry include a variety of Combat Engineers, Gunner squads, I-TOW, and TOW-2 ATGM teams. Tanks are still present, though limited in number and more expensive to deploy. These are the older M60A3 (TTS), early M1 Abrams with 105mm tank guns, and a handful of M1A1s. Artillery is potent, ranging from the M125 mortar carrier to the heavy M110A2 203mm self-propelled howitzer. The U.S. Air Force provides the modern F-16 Fighting Falcon in various loadouts for air cover. The improved F-111F makes its mark as a tactical bomber, including fielding a variant equipped with precision laser-guided bombs. "
"HISUS9Mot";"The 9th Infantry (Motorized) Division’s rich military history covered both World Wars and the Vietnam War. However, its uniqueness came to the forefront in 1981 when it became a special testbed formation for the U.S. Army. The 9th Infantry was envisioned to be light enough to deploy rapidly, but still deal with the heaviest threats. To accomplish this, it turned to an arsenal of highly advanced equipment, earning its nickname as the “Toys 'R' Us Division.” The battlegroup, with a heavy National Guard mechanized brigade, was destined to be deployed to Denmark, but with war on the horizon, would see itself redeploy into NORTHAG. \n\nThe 9th Infantry (Motorized) Division fields two new vehicle families, one being the CUCV utility truck, the other the HMMWV or Humvee. Both are used by the division’s Light Infantry and National Guard infantry in a great variety of roles, from the M1008 CUCV Supply to the M998T Interim Squad Carrier and the recon M1025 Humvee G/VLLD. A smorgasbord of exotic units includes the M198 155mm (CLGP) with Copperhead guided ammo, the M60A1 AVLM mine-clearing vehicle, the M1008 CUCV GLH with ground-launched Hellfire missiles, the JOH-58 recon helo, the towed anti-air XM895 T-CHAP, the MQM-10 Aquila UAV, and two-person Sniper teams fielding the iconic M82 anti-materiel sniper rifle."

"KMWLEKBPVE";"A tank gun is a large-caliber, high-velocity gun capable of firing various projectiles against a variety of targets.\nA tank gun is the primary means of engaging other tanks or armored vehicles with direct fire. Featuring different calibers, between 90mm to 125mm, a tank gun is often emplaced in a turret, creating a flexible yet hard-hitting weapon. When assisted by advanced targeting computers and sights, a tank gun can engage almost any kind of unit, even airborne targets, regardless of the weather or time of day. A tank gun fires off a variety of different shells, at times supported by an autoloader, including armor-piercing kinetic (AP), armor-piercing, fin-stabilized, discarding sabot (APFSDS), high-explosive (HE), or high-explosive anti-tank (HEAT). "SPTPUCUXQK";"A tank gun is a large-caliber, high-velocity gun capable of firing various projectiles against a variety of targets.\nA tank gun is the primary means of engaging other tanks or armored vehicles with direct fire. Featuring different calibers, between 90mm to 125mm, a tank gun is often emplaced in a turret, creating a flexible yet hard-hitting weapon. When assisted by advanced targeting computers and sights, a tank gun can engage almost any kind of unit, even airborne targets, regardless of the weather or time of day. A tank gun fires off a variety of different shells, at times supported by an autoloader, including armor-piercing kinetic (AP), armor-piercing, fin-stabilized, discarding sabot (APFSDS), high-explosive (HE), or high-explosive anti-tank (HEAT). Some guns can even fire specially adapted guided missiles. "

"YDWRGQLHYI";"A tank gun is a large-caliber, high-velocity gun capable of firing various projectiles against a variety of targets.\nA tank gun is the primary means of engaging other tanks or armored vehicles with direct fire. Featuring different calibers, between 90mm to 125mm, a tank gun is often emplaced in a turret, creating a flexible yet hard-hitting weapon. When assisted by advanced targeting computers and sights, a tank gun can engage almost any kind of unit, even airborne targets, regardless of the weather or time of day. A tank gun fires off a variety of different shells, at times supported by an autoloader, including armor-piercing kinetic (AP), armor-piercing, fin-stabilized, discarding sabot (APFSDS), high-explosive (HE), or high-explosive anti-tank (HEAT). Some guns can even fire specially adapted guided missiles. "
